The Mu'tazila: Later Innovations and the Call for Balance
Ibn Asakir points out the cause of the Mu'tazila's later innovations and quotes al-Khattabi's historical clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reason for the Mu'tazila's later innovations according to Ibn Asakir, and the distinction between early and later Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Excessive debate led the Mu'tazila to adopt innovations that later scholars rejected.

After praising the Mu'tazila's contributions, Ibn Asakir turns to their later deviations. He attributes these to their excessive engagement in debating opponents, which introduced erroneous ideas into their thought. He then quotes al-Khattabi to distinguish the early Mu'tazila from those who later introduced innovations. This lesson examines the boundary of their deviation.

Guided Path
1
Read the criticism
Pay attention to the cause-and-effect: their excessive debate led to stray ideas.
2
Understand the exception
The phrase 'لحقهم إلا أنهم' (they are to be followed except that...) shows they were generally followed but had this shortcoming.
3
Analyze al-Khattabi's quote
Al-Khattabi clarifies that the early Mu'tazila were not like later ones; innovations were introduced later.
This adds historical nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعتزلة على ضد الحشوية بخط مستقيم أنتجها البحث العلمي، ساقهم شره عقولهم إلى محاولة اكتناه كل شيء وعداؤهم الأصلي نحو الجمود وخطتهم دفع الآراء المتسربة من الخارج إلى الإسلام بحجج دامغة وأدلة عقلية مفحمة ولهم مواقف شريفة في الدفاع عن الدين الإسلامي إزاء الدهريين ومنكرى النبوة والثنوية والنصارى واليهود والصابئة وأصناف الملاحدة، وترى الذهبي يترحم على الجاحظ في سير النبلاء حين يذكر كتابه في النبوة، ولم نر مايقارب کتاب تثبيت دلائل النبوة للقاضي عبد الجبار (۱) في قوة الحجاج وحسن الصياغة فى دفع شكوك المشككين وليس بجيد الأعراض الكلى عن كتبهم وكم فيها من الفوائد التي لاتزال في أثوابها القشيبة لم تبل بكرور الزمن عليها . وكم كان الاستاذ الإمام يجاد فيها ما يدفع به خصوم العصر ولا يتحاشى عن الأخذ به من غير بخس . لحقهم إلا أنهم لكثرة استغالهم بمناظرة الاخصام عدت منهم إلى عقولهم آراء ابتعدوا بها عن الصواب وانغمسوا في بدع ردها الأصحاب، قال الخطابي صاحب معالم السنن : كانت المعتزلة فى الزمان الأول على خلاف هذه الأهواء وإنما أحدثها بعضهم في الزمان المتأخر.
And the Mu'tazila are the direct opposite of the Hashwiyya, produced by scholarly research. Their greed for [the use of] their minds drove them to attempt to comprehend everything, and their original enmity was towards rigidity. Their plan was to repel the ideas that seeped into Islam from outside with conclusive proofs and overwhelming rational evidence. They have honorable stances in defending the Islamic religion against the materialists (dahriyyun), deniers of prophethood, dualists, Christians, Jews, Sabians, and all kinds of atheists. You see al-Dhahabi praying for mercy for al-Jahiz in Siyar al-Nubala' when he mentions his book on prophethood. And we have not seen anything approaching the book 'Tathbit Dala'il al-Nubuwwa' of Qadi Abd al-Jabbar in strength of argument and good composition in repelling the doubts of skeptics. And it is not good to completely turn away from their books; how many benefits are in them that still remain in their fresh garments, not worn out by the passage of time. And how often did the teacher imam (likely Ibn Asakir's teacher) debate with them, taking what repels the opponents of the age, not refraining from taking it without detracting. They are to be followed [in that], except that due to their excessive occupation with debating opponents, ideas entered their minds that strayed from correctness, and they immersed themselves in innovations that the scholars rejected. Al-Khattabi, author of Ma'alim al-Sunan, said: 'The Mu'tazila in the early period were different from these inclinations; only some of them later invented them in the later period.'
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents a nuanced evaluation of the Mu'tazila. The author begins by stating that the Mu'tazila are the direct opposite of the Hashwiyya, born from scholarly research. He acknowledges their intellectual drive to understand everything and their initial opposition to rigidity. Their project was to defend Islam from external ideas using rational arguments. He praises their efforts against various opponents, and even notes that al-Dhahabi sympathized with al-Jahiz's book on prophethood. He highly praises the book 'Tathbit Dala'il al-Nubuwwa' by Qadi Abd al-Jabbar for its strength and composition. He cautions against completely discarding their works, as they contain lasting benefits. He mentions that his own teacher would use their arguments to refute contemporary opponents without hesitation. However, he points out that their excessive engagement with opponents led to some of them adopting erroneous ideas and innovations, which later scholars rejected. He then quotes al-Khattabi to reinforce that the early Mu'tazila were not like the later ones who introduced innovations. Thus, the author gives credit where due but also marks the boundary of their deviation.

Key Terms
بدع
خطابي
معالم السنن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Mu'tazila were always innovated and had no good aspects.
Correction: Ibn Asakir and al-Khattabi show that the early Mu'tazila were praiseworthy; innovations only occurred later due to excessive debate.

Checkpoint
According to al-Khattabi as quoted, when did the Mu'tazila's innovations arise?
A) In the earliest period.
B) In the later period from some members.
C) They always had them.
D) They never had innovations.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's later innovations were a result of excessive debate, but early Mu'tazila were not blameworthy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in debates about religion, are you doing so to seek truth or to win? How can you ensure that your own desire to debate does not lead you away from the correct path as it did for the later Mu'tazila?
?
The author notes that the early Mu'tazila were different from the later ones. In your own practice of Islam, are you being influenced by voices that claim to be rational but actually introduce innovations? How can you distinguish between legitimate reasoning and stray ideas?
?
Reflect on a time when your own excessive argumentation caused you to adopt a view that was not sound. What can you learn from the Mu'tazila's mistake to humble yourself before the truth?

The Ash'ariyya as the Just Middle Path
Ibn Asakir characterizes the Ash'ariyya as balanced between reason and revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ariyya are described as the balanced middle path between the extreme sects of the Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya.

Core Idea
The Ash'ariyya harmonize reason and revelation, avoiding the extremes of the Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya.

Ibn Asakir presents a concise definition of the Ash'ari school, positioning it as the just middle between two problematic extremes. The Mu'tazila overemphasized reason at the expense of transmitted revelation, while the Hashwiyya rejected reason altogether. This short passage captures the essence of Ash'ari methodology: a balanced integration of both sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation without pausing to analyze. Let the author's phrasing settle in your mind.
Notice that the passage ends mid-sentence; we have only the opening portion.
2
Identify the two extremes
The passage names two sects: the Mu'tazila and the Hashwiyya. Note what each is said to have done wrong according to Ibn Asakir.
Mu'tazila: departed from transmitted revelation. Hashwiyya: abandoned reason.
3
Understand the Ash'ari position
The Ash'ariyya are described as the 'just middle' because they did not commit either error. They preserved both revelation and reason.
The phrase 'لا ابتعدوا عن النقل ولا عن العقل' (they did not depart from revelation nor from reason) is key.
4
Reflect on the outcome
The passage states that the Ash'aris inherited the good of earlier scholars, rejected falsehood, and preserved the Prophet's way. Consider how this follows from their balanced methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأشعرية هم العدل الوسط بين المعتزلة والحشوية لا ابتعدوا عن النقل كما فعل المعتزلة ولا عن العقل كعادة الحشوية، ورثوا خير من تقدمهم وهجروا باطل كل فرقة، حافظوا على ما كان عليه النبي صلى الله
And the Ash'ariyya are the just middle between the Mu'tazila and the Hashwiyya: they did not depart from transmitted revelation as the Mu'tazila did, nor from reason as is the habit of the Hashwiyya. They inherited the good of those before them and abandoned the falsehood of every sect. They preserved [the way] upon which the Prophet (may God bless him and grant him peace) ...
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash'ariyya as the balanced school. The author states they are the 'just middle' ('العدل الوسط') between the two extremes: the Mu'tazila, who overemphasized reason and departed from transmitted revelation, and the Hashwiyya, who rejected reason and followed only literal interpretations. The Ash'aris combine both reason and revelation. They inherited the good from earlier schools and rejected the falsehood of each sect. They preserved the way of the Prophet. The text is cut off, but the main idea is clear: the Ash'ariyya represent the orthodox Sunni position that harmonizes reason and revelation.

Key Terms
أشعرية
عدل وسط
معتزلة
حشوية
نقل
عقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ariyya are purely rationalist like the Mu'tazila.
Correction: Ibn Asakir clarifies that they did not depart from transmitted revelation; they balance it with reason.

Checkpoint
In what sense does Ibn Asakir describe the Ash'ariyya as the 'just middle'?
A) They are between the Hashwiyya and the Khawarij.
B) They use both reason and transmitted revelation, avoiding the extremes of the Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya.
C) They are politically neutral.
D) They are moderate in jurisprudence.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ariyya are defined as the balanced school that combines reason and revelation, avoiding the extremes of the Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own relationship with your faith, do you lean more toward rationalizing everything until revelation bends to your mind, or do you accept teachings without ever engaging your intellect? Which extreme do you tend toward, and what would it look like to walk the 'just middle' like the Ash'ariyya?
?
Ibn Asakir says the Ash'ariyya 'inherited the good of those before them and abandoned the falsehood of every sect.' Think of the people you look up to or the groups you follow. What 'good' have you genuinely inherited from them, and what 'falsehood' have you consciously rejected? Are you willing to abandon falsehood even when it comes from a source you respect?
?
The Ash'ariyya 'preserved the way of the Prophet.' Ask yourself: Do you actively preserve the prophetic way in your daily life, or have you allowed cultural habits, personal convenience, or peer pressure to dilute that path? What is one specific practice you can restore or strengthen starting today?

The Summaniyya and Barahima: Sects of Permissiveness and Obscurity
Ibn Asakir identifies Summaniyya and Barahima as sects of permissiveness and obscurity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the characterization of the Summaniyya and Barahima as sects of permissiveness and obscurity.

Core Idea
Summaniyya and Barahima represent destructive permissiveness and obscurity.

Ibn Asakir opens his discussion of deviant sects by grouping two groups together: the Summaniyya and the Barahima. He labels them as sects of permissiveness (ibaha) and obscurity (khumul). This lesson explores what that classification implies about their beliefs and practices.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Summaniyya and Barahima
Read the Arabic and translation for the first part of the passage, focusing on the terms used to describe these two sects.
Note the word 'ghayrihima' indicating other similar sects are included.
2
Analyze the terms 'ibaha' and 'khumul'
Consider what 'permissiveness' and 'obscurity' mean in a theological context. 'Ibaha often implies antinomianism, while 'khumul suggests being obscure or unknown.
3
Reflect on the grouping
Ask yourself why Ibn Asakir groups these two sects together. What common traits do they share?
They are both characterized by deviation from mainstream Islamic norms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمنية والبراهمة وغيرهما من فرق الاباحة والخمول . والقدرية نشأت من بحث علمى ووجهتها نحو خصومه الكسل والتواكل وباعتبار ما تطور اليها متأثرة ببعض آراء الثنوية . والحشوية أسقطها الجهل والجمود ترتئى آراء جاهلية ورثتها من نحل كانوا عليها قبل الإسلام وراحت عليهم تمويهات المموهين من الثنوية وأهل الكتاب والصائبة، لهم تقشف يخدعون به العامة وجهالات لا يتصورها عاقل وهو غلاظ الطباع قساة جنماة يتحينون الفرص لاحداث القلاقل لا يظهر لهم قول الا عند ضعف الاسلام ويستفحل أمر الالحاد مع ظهور قولهم هكذا في جميع ادوار التاريخ، خصومتهم متوجهة نحو العقل والعلوم النظرية وكل فرقة قائمة.
The Summaniyya and the Barahima and others from the sects of permissiveness and obscurity. And the Qadariyya originated from a scientific inquiry, and its orientation was towards its opponents [who are characterized by] laziness and reliance, and considering what it developed into, influenced by some opinions of the Dualists. And the Hashwiyya: ignorance and stagnation caused them to fall; they hold pre-Islamic ignorant opinions that they inherited from cults they were upon before Islam, and the deceptions of the deceivers from the Dualists, the People of the Book, and the Sabians prevailed over them. They have asceticism by which they deceive the common people, and ignorances that no rational person can imagine. They are coarse-natured, harsh, eager for opportunities to cause turmoil; their opinion does not appear except when Islam is weak, and the matter of atheism intensifies with the appearance of their saying, thus in all periods of history. Their hostility is directed towards reason and theoretical sciences, and every sect persists.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage classifies several deviant sects. It begins with the Summaniyya and Barahima, noting they are sects of permissiveness and obscurity. Then the Qadariyya: they originated from scientific inquiry but became influenced by dualist ideas. The Hashwiyya are described as ignorant and stagnant, holding pre-Islamic beliefs, deceived by dualists and others. They are coarse and opportunistic, only manifesting when Islam is weak. Their hostility is towards reason and theoretical knowledge. The passage ends with 'and every sect persists,' likely indicating that these groups continue to exist.

Key Terms
السمنية
البراهمة
الاباحة
الخمول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, how does he categorize the Summaniyya and Barahima?
A) As sects of reason and science
B) As sects of permissiveness and obscurity
C) As sects of dualism
D) As sects of asceticism

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir characterizes the Summaniyya and Barahima as groups defined by permissiveness and obscurity, indicating a fundamental deviation from Islamic norms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Asakir warns of sects that combine permissiveness (outward rejection of obligations) with obscurity (hiddenness). In your own life, are there areas where you outwardly reject God's commands (permissiveness) or secretly rationalize sins (obscurity)? Which one are you more prone to, and what specific step will you take this week to confront it?
?
The Barahima and Summaniyya are described as 'obscure'—their errors are hidden from public view. What sin or wrong belief do you keep hidden from others because you don't want to be held accountable? How does hiding it make it more dangerous, and what would change if you brought it into the light of sincere repentance?

The Qadariyya: Origins and Dualist Influence
Ibn Asakir traces the Qadariyya's origins and their corruption by dualist ideas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's claim that the Qadariyya originated from scientific inquiry but later became influenced by dualist ideas.

Core Idea
Qadariyya began with inquiry but fell into dualist corruption.

Ibn Asakir next turns to the Qadariyya, noting that they originated from a scientific inquiry but then shifted towards laziness and reliance, eventually being influenced by dualists. This lesson examines this trajectory and what it reveals about the sect's deviance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Qadariyya
Read the Arabic and translation for the Qadariyya section carefully, noting the sequence: origin, development, and influence.
The phrase 'بحث علمى' indicates a theoretical starting point.
2
Identify the shift
Notice how the Qadariyya's orientation turned towards its opponents, who are described as lazy and reliant. This suggests a polemical focus.
3
Consider the dualist influence
Reflect on what 'influenced by some opinions of the Dualists' means. Dualists likely refer to Zoroastrians or Manichaeans, who held a dualistic view of good and evil.
This indicates theological corruption.

?

The Hashwiyya: Ignorance, Stagnation, and Hostility to Reason
Ibn Asakir provides a detailed critique of the Hashwiyya sect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's detailed critique of the Hashwiyya as ignorant, stagnant, and hostile to reason and theoretical sciences.

Core Idea
Hashwiyya embody ignorance, deception, and war on reason.

Ibn Asakir devotes the longest description to the Hashwiyya, portraying them as a sect ruined by ignorance and stagnation. They hold pre-Islamic beliefs, deceive the public with asceticism, and are hostile to reason. This lesson unpacks this multifaceted critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Hashwiyya
Read the entire Arabic and translation for the Hashwiyya section, noting the different traits mentioned.
This is a dense passage with many accusations.
2
Identify the causes
Ibn Asakir says ignorance (jahl) and stagnation (jumud) caused their fall. Then he lists their inherited pre-Islamic beliefs and deception by others.
3
Analyze their character
Note the description of their nature (coarse, harsh), their opportunism, and their hostility towards reason and theoretical sciences. Consider why this hostility is highlighted.
This shows they are anti-intellectual.
4
Summarize the sect's pattern
Ibn Asakir claims their opinion only appears when Islam is weak, and atheism intensifies with their saying. This suggests a cyclical pattern.

D) During scholarly debates

Key Takeaway
The Hashwiyya are characterized by ignorance, pre-Islamic beliefs, deceptive asceticism, and a persistent hostility towards reason and theoretical sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to a belief simply because it was inherited, without questioning whether it aligns with the truth? Examine one area of your faith where you might be practicing stagnation (jumud) rather than seeking understanding.
?
In what ways might you be using outward piety or asceticism (taqashshuf) to gain the approval of people rather than sincerely drawing closer to Allah? Confront any hypocrisy you find and resolve to purify your intention.
?
Are you, like the Hashwiyya, harsh in nature (ghaliz al-tibaa') and quick to cause division when you feel your views are threatened? Commit today to softening your heart and seeking unity, even when you disagree.

A Balanced View of the Mu'tazila: Merits and Errors
Ibn Asakir describes the Mu'tazila's origins, strengths, and weaknesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's nuanced assessment of the Mu'tazila, including their strengths in defending Islam and the development of their later innovations.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila combined intellectual rigor with later excess, requiring a balanced judgment.

Ibn Asakir presents a sophisticated portrait of the Mu'tazila, avoiding both wholesale condemnation and uncritical praise. He acknowledges their role in defending Islam against external ideologies and their scholarly contributions, while also recognizing that excessive engagement with opponents led some of them into innovative errors. This passage sets the stage for a fair evaluation of the sect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the balanced tone from the start.
Ibn Asakir uses the phrase 'على ضد الحشوية' to contrast them.
2
Identify the positive points
List the merits Ibn Asakir mentions: intellectual pursuit, defense against various groups, praise for specific scholars like al-Jahiz and al-Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar, and the value of their books.
The passage even quotes al-Dhahabi showing mercy on al-Jahiz.
3
Identify the criticisms
Find where Ibn Asakir introduces the negative: excessive debate led to wrong opinions and innovations. Note the quote from al-Khattabi distinguishing early from later Mu'tazila.
The criticism is introduced with 'لحقهم إلا أنهم...'.
4
Reflect on the balanced methodology
Consider why Ibn Asakir presents both sides and how this reflects a scholarly approach to studying sectarian differences.
This lesson's core idea is about balance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعتزلة على ضد الحشوية بخط مستقيم أنتجها البحث العلمي، ساقهم شره عقولهم إلى محاولة اكتناه كل شيء وعداؤهم الأصلي نحو الجمود وخطتهم دفع الآراء المتسربة من الخارج إلى الإسلام بحجج دامغة وأدلة عقلية مفحمة ولهم مواقف شريفة في الدفاع عن الدين الإسلامي إزاء الدهريين ومنكرى النبوة والثنوية والنصارى واليهود والصابئة وأصناف الملاحدة، وترى الذهبي يترحم على الجاحظ في سير النبلاء حين يذكر كتابه في النبوة، ولم نر مايقارب کتاب تثبيت دلائل النبوة للقاضي عبد الجبار (۱) في قوة الحجاج وحسن الصياغة فى دفع شكوك المشككين وليس بجيد الأعراض الكلى عن كتبهم وكم فيها من الفوائد التي لاتزال في أثوابها القشيبة لم تبل بكرور الزمن عليها . وكم كان الاستاذ الإمام يجاد فيها ما يدفع به خصوم العصر ولا يتحاشى عن الأخذ به من غير بخس . لحقهم إلا أنهم لكثرة استغالهم بمناظرة الاخصام عدت منهم إلى عقولهم آراء ابتعدوا بها عن الصواب وانغمسوا في بدع ردها الأصحاب، قال الخطابي صاحب معالم السنن : كانت المعتزلة فى الزمان الأول على خلاف هذه الأهواء وإنما أحدثها بعضهم في الزمان المتأخر.
And the Mu'tazila, opposite to the Hashwiyya, on a straight line, produced by scientific inquiry. Their intellectual greed drove them to attempt to fathom everything, and their original enmity was towards stagnation, and their plan was to repel the opinions that infiltrated into Islam from outside with conclusive arguments and overwhelming rational proofs. They have noble positions in defending the Islamic religion against the materialists, deniers of prophethood, dualists, Christians, Jews, Sabians, and various kinds of atheists. And you see al-Dhahabi asking for mercy upon al-Jahiz in Siyar al-Nubala' when he mentions his book on prophethood. And we have not seen anything approaching the book 'Tathbit Dala'il al-Nubuwwa' of al-Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar in strength of argumentation and beauty of composition in repelling the doubts of skeptics. And it is not good to completely ignore their books, for how many benefits are in them that remain in their elegant garments, not worn out by the passage of time. And how often did the teacher-imam [Ibn Asakir?] argue with them to repel the opponents of the age, and he did not shy away from taking from them without detraction. However, due to their excessive engagement in debating opponents, opinions penetrated into their minds that distanced them from correctness, and they immersed themselves in innovations that the companions rejected. Al-Khattabi, author of Ma'alim al-Sunan, said: 'The Mu'tazila in the early period were contrary to these passions; only some of them innovated them in the later period.'
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage provides a balanced assessment of the Mu'tazila. It begins by stating they are the opposite of the Hashwiyya, on a straight line produced by scientific inquiry. Their intellectual greed led them to try to understand everything, and their original enmity was towards stagnation. Their plan was to use conclusive arguments to repel foreign ideas from Islam. They are praised for defending Islam against various groups: materialists, deniers of prophethood, dualists, Christians, Jews, Sabians, and atheists. The author notes that even al-Dhahabi had mercy on al-Jahiz, and he praises al-Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar's book on proof of prophethood. He argues against completely ignoring their works due to their benefits. However, he also points out that due to excessive debate, some wrong opinions entered their minds, leading to innovations. He quotes al-Khattabi who says that early Mu'tazila were not like these later innovators.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir balances the Mu'tazila's significant contributions in defending Islam with their later innovations, urging a nuanced understanding rather than blanket rejection.

?

?
Are you quick to label an entire group based on the errors of some of its later members? How can you adopt a more balanced judgment like Ibn Asakir, recognizing early merits while rejecting later innovations?

The Ash'ariyya: The Balanced Middle Path
Ibn Asakir describes the Ash'ariyya as the balanced middle path between Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir characterizes the Ash'ariyya as a balanced middle school between reason and revelation, and how he evaluates al-Ash'ari's contributions with moderation.

Core Idea
The Ash'ariyya is the just middle, preserving both revelation and reason.

Ibn Asakir presents the Ash'ariyya not as a fringe sect but as the balanced mainstream. He contrasts them with two extremes: the Mu'tazila who overemphasized reason and the Hashwiyya who clung to literal revelation without reason. This passage explains their methodology and gives a fair assessment of al-Ash'ari himself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage first, then the English translation. Let the author's own words set the stage before you analyze.
The passage is a single coherent paragraph; read it through without pausing.
2
Identify the two extremes and the middle
Notice how Ibn Asakir defines the Ash'ariyya as the just middle between the Mu'tazila and the Hashwiyya. What did each extreme neglect?
Mu'tazila: distanced from revelation. Hashwiyya: distanced from reason.
3
Observe the connection to Sufism
The passage mentions that some Ash'aris are also Sufis, due to the support of Sufi imams for the Sunni method since the fifth century. This shows a historical link.
4
Understand the balanced critique of al-Ash'ari
Ibn Asakir praises al-Ash'ari's unparalleled work but admits his opinions are not free from some objections. Note the reason given: his long debates with Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya inevitably affected his speech.
This is a nuanced evaluation, neither deifying nor dismissing.
5
Reflect on the lesson's significance
Think about how this passage positions the Ash'ariyya in Sunni theology: as a moderate, mainstream school that values both scripture and intellect, and as a tradition that acknowledges its own critical history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأشعرية هم العدل الوسط بين المعتزلة والحشوية لا ابتعدوا عن النقل كما فعل المعتزلة ولا عن العقل كعادة الحشوية، ورثوا خير من تقدمهم وهجروا باطل كل فرقة، حافظوا على ما كان عليه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه وملأوا العالم علما، ويوجد بنهم من ينتمى إلى التصوف من مناصرة بعض الأئمة من الصوفية للسنة على الطريقة الأشعرية منذ القرن الخامس. ولا يوجد من يوازن الأشعرى بين المتكلمين بالنظر لما قام به من العمل العظيم ومع ذلك لا تخلو آراؤه من بعض ما يؤخذ كنوع ابتعاد عن العقل مرة وعن النقل أخرى في حسبان الناظر في كلامه في مسائل نظرية معدودة كقوله في التحسين والتقبيح والتعليل ومايفيده الدليل النقلى ونحو ذلك لأن من طال جداله مع أصناف المعتزلة والحشوية مثله لابد وان يحصل في كلامه شيء من هذا القبيل .
And the Ash'ariyya are the just middle between the Mu'tazila and the Hashwiyya: they did not distance from transmitted revelation as the Mu'tazila did, nor from reason as is the habit of the Hashwiyya. They inherited the best of those before them and abandoned the falsehood of every sect. They preserved what the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions were upon, and they filled the world with knowledge. Among them are those who ascribe to Sufism, due to the support of some Sufi imams for the Sunna on the Ash'ari method since the fifth century. And there is no one among the theologians who equals al-Ash'ari in view of the great work he accomplished. Nevertheless, his opinions are not free from some objections that are seen as a kind of distance from reason at times and from transmitted revelation at other times in the estimation of one who examines his speech in certain theoretical issues, like his statement on al-tahsin wa al-taqbih (the intrinsic goodness and badness of actions) and al-ta'lil (causation) and what the transmitted proof indicates, and the like. That is because one who has long debated with various kinds of Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya, like him, inevitably some things of this sort occur in his speech.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage defines the Ash'ariyya as the just middle between the Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya. They neither abandoned transmitted revelation (nasql) like the Mu'tazila, nor reason like the Hashwiyya. They inherited the best from predecessors and rejected falsehood. They preserved the Sunnah and filled the world with knowledge. The passage also notes the connection between Ash'arism and Sufism since the fifth century. Then it evaluates al-Ash'ari himself: he is unmatched among theologians for his great work, but his opinions are not entirely free from criticism, particularly in issues like tahsin wa taqbih (moral evaluation of actions), ta'lil (causation), and the implications of transmitted proofs. This is attributed to the inevitable effect of his long debates with Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Ash'ari was infallible and his views are beyond critique.
Correction: Ibn Asakir acknowledges that his long debates led to some debatable positions, but this does not diminish his immense contributions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did some of al-Ash'ari's opinions become objectionable?
A) He was not well-versed in theology
B) His long debates with Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya affected his speech
C) He deliberately abandoned reason
D) He followed the Hashwiyya

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ariyya maintain a balanced approach, incorporating both revelation and reason, and al-Ash'ari's work is admired despite minor critiques due to his polemical context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own understanding of Islam, do you tend to rely more on reason or on transmitted texts? Where do you fall on the spectrum between the Mu'tazila and the Hashwiyya? What practical steps can you take today to ensure you follow the 'just middle' as the Ash'ariyya did?
?
Al-Ash'ari, despite his great work, had positions that were subject to critique. Do you ever idolize scholars to the point of ignoring their possible errors? How can you appreciate their contributions while still maintaining critical thinking and humility?
?
The Ash'ariyya preserved both reason and revelation. How have you personally neglected one over the other? What change will you make this week to restore balance in your practice of Islam?

The Maturidiyya: Complete Moderation and Verbal Differences
Ibn Asakir describes the Maturidiyya as the balanced school between Ash'ariyya and Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Maturidi was able to achieve complete moderation in his theological views and how his school relates to the Ash'ariyya.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi's moderation stemmed from the dominance of Sunna; his school is the middle path.

Ibn Asakir contrasts the circumstances of Imam al-Ash'ari and Imam al-Maturidi to highlight a key difference in their contexts. While al-Ash'ari faced intense polemics, al-Maturidi worked in a region where the Sunna was overwhelmingly dominant, allowing him to balance transmitted revelation and reason more freely. This passage explains the unique character of the Maturidiyya and clarifies that their disagreements with the Ash'ariyya are mostly verbal.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical context
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand why al-Maturidi's environment was different from al-Ash'ari's. Focus on the phrase 'لتغلب السنة هناك' (because the Sunna was dominant).
Notice that this dominance prevented disturbances from innovators.
2
Identify the characterization of Maturidiyya
Ibn Asakir describes the Maturidiyya as 'الوسط بين الأشاعرة والمعتزلة' (the middle between Ash'ariyya and Mu'tazila). Also note the rare presence of Sufis among them.
3
Understand the nature of disagreements
The passage states that most differences between al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi are of the type 'الخلاف اللفظى' (verbal dispute). Reflect on why this is significant.
This leads to the conclusion that both are imams of Ahl al-Sunna worldwide.
4
Explore the scholarly tradition
Read the mention of al-Bayadi's 'Isharat al-Maram' and its transmission by al-Zabidi. Note al-Maqbili's respect for al-Bayadi despite his difficult character.
This shows the enduring value of the Maturidi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما لم يقع مثل ذلك في معاصرة إمام الهدى أبى منصور الماتريدى شيخ السنة بما وراء النهر لتغلب السنة هناك على أصناف المبتدعة تغلبا تاما لا تظهر مشاغباتهم معه، فتمكن من الجرى على الاعتدال التام فى أنظاره فأعطى النقل حقه والعقل حكمه والماتريدية هم الوسط بين الأشاعرة والمعتزلة وقلما يوجد بينهم متصوف فالأشعرى والماتريدى هما إماما أهل السنة والجماعة في مشارق الأرض ومغاربها لهم كتب لاتحصى، وغالب ما وقع بين هذين الإمامين من الخلاف من قبيل الخلاف اللفظى، وقد دونت عدة كتب في ذلك، وقد أحسن تلخيصها البياضي فى اشارات المرام في عبارات الإمام ) ونقل نصه الزبيدى فى شرح الإحياء على أغلاط مطبيعية كثيرة، والبياضي هذا ضليع في علم الكلام وإن تأخر زمنه حتى ان المقبلي صاحب العلم الشامخ على جموحه وصعوبة انقياده للعلماء كبير العناية باشارات البياضى اعترافا منه بسعة دائرة بحثه
And such [objections] did not occur in the contemporary of Imam al-Huda Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, the Shaykh of the Sunna in Transoxiana, because the Sunna was fully dominant there over the various types of innovators, so their disturbances did not appear against him. Thus he was able to pursue complete moderation in his views: he gave transmitted revelation its right and reason its ruling. And the Maturidiyya are the middle between the Ash'ariyya and the Mu'tazila, and rarely does one find among them a Sufi. So al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi are the two imams of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a in the east of the earth and the west. They have innumerable books. And most of the disagreement between these two imams is of the type of verbal dispute (khilaf lafzi). Several books have been written on that, and al-Bayadi well summarized them in 'Isharat al-Maram fi 'Ibarat al-Imam', and al-Zabidi transmitted his text in his commentary on al-Ihya' with many typographical errors. And this al-Bayadi was proficient in kalam, even though his time was late, such that al-Maqbili, author of 'al-'Ilm al-Shamikh', despite his obstinacy and difficulty in submitting to scholars, paid great attention to al-Bayadi's 'Isharat', acknowledging the breadth of his research.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage contrasts al-Maturidi with al-Ash'ari. It notes that al-Maturidi did not face the same polemical pressures because Sunnism was completely dominant in Transoxiana, allowing him to maintain perfect moderation, giving both transmitted revelation and reason their due. The Maturidiyya are the middle between Ash'ariyya and Mu'tazila, and rarely include Sufis. Both al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi are the imams of Ahl al-Sunna worldwide, with countless books. Their differences are mostly verbal (khilaf lafzi). The passage then mentions al-Bayadi's summary 'Isharat al-Maram', which al-Zabidi transmitted with many typographical errors. Despite his late era, al-Bayadi was proficient in kalam, and even the difficult al-Maqbili highly valued his work.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidiyya represent a balanced theological school that emerged in an environment of Sunni dominance, and their disagreements with the Ash'ariyya are largely verbal, preserving unity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Are you willing to investigate and perhaps let go of that division for the sake of unity—what would that cost you?
?

Ash'ari and Maturidi: The Two Imams of Ahl al-Sunna
Ibn 'Asakir compares Ash'ari and Maturidi, concluding both are imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn 'Asakir portrays al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi as the two imams of Ahl al-Sunna, highlighting their respective contexts and contributions.

Core Idea
Ash'ari and Maturidi are the twin pillars of Sunni theology.

Ibn 'Asakir provides a balanced comparison between these two foundational figures. He acknowledges al-Ash'ari's great work while noting some criticisms, and contrasts him with al-Maturidi, who enjoyed a more favorable environment for his moderate approach. This passage establishes both as authoritative imams for Sunni Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to understand the overall comparison.
Notice the structure: first Ash'ari, then Maturidi, then conclusion.
2
Identify the description of al-Ash'ari
Find how Ibn 'Asakir describes al-Ash'ari's status and the criticisms mentioned. Why are there criticisms?
The criticisms are linked to his debates with the Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya.
3

See how al-Maturidi's context in Transoxiana allowed him to be more moderate. Note the phrase 'gave transmitted evidence its due and reason its judgment'.
The Maturidis are described as the middle between Ash'arites and Mu'tazila.
4

ويوجد فيهم من ينتمي إلى التصوف من مناصرة بعض الأئمة من الصوفية للسنة على الطريقة الأشعرية منذ القرن الخامس. ولا يوجد من يوازن الأشعري بين المتكلمين بالنظر لما قام به من العمل العظيم ومع ذلك لا تخلو آراؤه من بعض ما يؤخذ كنوع ابتعاد عن العقل مرة وعن النقل أخرى في حسبان الناظر في كلامه في مسائل نظرية معدودة كقوله في التحسين والتقبيح والتعليل وما يفيده الدليل النقلي ونحو ذلك لأن من طال جداله مع أصناف المعتزلة والحشوية مثله لابد أن يحصل في كلامه شيء من هذا القبيل. وإنما لم يقع مثل ذلك في معاصرة إمام الهدى أبي منصور الماتريدي شيخ السنة بما وراء النهر لتغلب السنة هناك على أصناف المبتدعة تغلبًا تامًا لا تظهر مشاغباتهم معه، فتمكن من الجري على الاعتدال التام في أنظاره فأعطى النقل حقه والعقل حكمه والماتريدية هم الوسط بين الأشاعرة والمعتزلة وقلما يوجد بينهم متصوف فالأشعري والماتريدي هما إماما أهل السنة والجماعة في مشارق الأرض ومغاربها لهم كتب لا تحصى، وغالب ما وقع بين هذين الإمامين من الخلاف من قبيل الخلاف اللفظي، وقد دونت عدة كتب في ذلك، وقد أحسن تلخيصها البياضي في إشارات المرام في عبارات الإمام) ونقل نصه الزبيدي في شرح الإحياء على أغلاط مطبعية كثيرة، والبياضي هذا ضليع في علم الكلام وإن تأخر زمنه حتى أن المقبلي صاحب العلم الشامخ على جموحه وصعوبة انقياده للعلماء كبير العناية بإشارات البياضي اعترافًا منه بسعة دائرة بحثه
Among them there are those who affiliate with Sufism, from the supporters of some Sufi imams of the Sunna on the Ash'ari way since the fifth century. There is no one who balances al-Ash'ari among the theologians (mutakallimun) considering the great work he did, and yet his opinions are not free from some criticisms as a kind of distancing from reason at times and from transmitted evidence at other times, in the view of the one looking into his speech in certain theoretical issues, such as his statement on al-tahsin wa al-taqbih (approval and disapproval) and ta'lil (causation) and what is indicated by transmitted evidence and the like, because one who argued extensively with various groups of Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya like him inevitably has something of this sort in his speech. But such did not occur for the contemporary of the Imam of Guidance Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, the Shaykh of the Sunna in Transoxiana, because the Sunna was so dominant there over the various sects of innovators that their obstreperousness did not appear with him. So he was able to proceed with complete moderation in his views, giving transmitted evidence its due and reason its judgment. The Maturidis are the middle between the Ash'arites and the Mu'tazila, and rarely is there a Sufi among them. So al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi are the two Imams of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a in the East and West of the earth; they have countless books. Most of the disagreement between these two Imams is of the type of verbal disagreement (al-khilaf al-lafzi), and several books have been written on that. al-Bayadi has ably summarized them in 'Isharat al-Maram fi 'Ibarat al-Imam' and al-Zabidi quoted him in his commentary on al-Ihya with many typographical errors. al-Bayadi is well-versed in kalam even though his time is later, to the extent that al-Muqabili, author of 'al-Ilm al-Shamikh', despite his stubbornness and difficulty in submitting to scholars, had great care for al-Bayadi's 'Isharat', acknowledging the breadth of his research.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is an evaluative comparison between al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi. It begins by noting that there are Sufis who support the Ash'ari way. Then it praises al-Ash'ari's great work but also acknowledges criticisms of his views in certain theoretical issues, such as his positions on tahsin wa taqbih (moral approval/disapproval) and ta'lil (causation), attributing these to his extensive debates with the Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya. It then contrasts al-Maturidi, who, due to the dominance of the Sunna in Transoxiana, could maintain perfect moderation, giving both transmitted evidence and reason their due. The Maturidis are described as the middle between the Ash'arites and the Mu'tazila, and it is noted that Sufis are rare among them. Both are affirmed as imams of Ahl al-Sunna, and their differences are mostly verbal. The passage concludes by mentioning al-Bayadi's summary of these differences and the care al-Muqabili had for his work, despite his stubbornness.

Key Terms
الأشعري
الماتريدي
أهل السنة والجماعة
التحسين والتقبيح
التعليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that al-Ash'ari's criticisms mean he is not a reliable imam.
Correction: The passage clarifies that criticisms are due to his debates with extremists and do not diminish his status as an imam of Ahl al-Sunna.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn 'Asakir, why does al-Ash'ari's speech contain some criticisms?
A) Because he argued extensively with Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya.
B) Because he was not knowledgeable.
C) Because he rejected transmitted evidence.
D) Because he was a Sufi.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi are both revered as imams of Ahl al-Sunna, despite differences in their contexts and minor critiques.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear that a respected scholar had certain flaws or criticisms, do you immediately dismiss them or do you consider the context that shaped their views? How does this lesson's attitude toward al-Ash'ari challenge the way you handle the imperfections of scholars you look up to?
?
Al-Maturidi was able to practice complete moderation because his environment was supportive of the Sunna. Are you in a context that helps or hinders your religious moderation? What practical step can you take to emulate al-Maturidi's balance, especially when you face opposition?
?
Both al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi are affirmed as imams of Ahl al-Sunna despite their differences. Is there someone from a different background whom you respect in theory but struggle to accept as part of the same community? How can this lesson's inclusive verdict transform your attitude toward them?

The Verbal Nature of Ash'ari-Maturidi Differences
Ibn 'Asakir states that most differences are verbal and mentions al-Bayadi's summary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that most disagreements between the Ash'ari and Maturidi schools are verbal (khilaf lafzi) and that scholars have compiled works to clarify them.

Core Idea
The differences between Ash'ari and Maturidi are mostly about words, not substance.

After establishing both as imams, Ibn 'Asakir addresses the nature of their disagreements. He states that they are largely verbal, and mentions the scholarly efforts to catalog them, specifically the work of al-Bayadi. This reassures students that the schools are united in core doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on verbal disagreement
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the statement that most differences are verbal.
The phrase 'al-khilaf al-lafzi' is key.
2
Understand 'khilaf lafzi'
Reflect on what it means for a disagreement to be verbal. It implies that the underlying positions are not contradictory.
This concept is important in Islamic theology to promote unity.
3
Note the scholarly works mentioned
Identify the books written on this topic, especially al-Bayadi's 'Isharat al-Maram' and its recognition by al-Muqabili.
This shows the importance of studying these differences.

Scope and Key Texts on Sectarian Differences
Author defines his methodological scope and lists authoritative books on sectarian views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's focus on the root sects and the key classical texts that document their views.

Core Idea
Reliable knowledge of sects begins with trustworthy sources.

The author begins by clarifying his method: he only addresses the basic sects, not their countless branches. He then lists the essential books that scholars have relied on for accurate information. This lesson establishes the foundation for proper study of heretical groups.

Guided Path
1
Read the scope statement
The first sentence limits the discussion to the roots of sects, acknowledging the existence of many branches. Notice the phrase 'أصول الفرق'.
The author is deliberate about not covering every branch.
2
Note the role of scholars
The passage states that scholars in every generation have detailed and refuted the views of sectarians. This shows a continuous scholarly effort.
3
Identify the key books
Find the list of books by al-Ash'ari, al-Maturidi, al-Tara'ifi, and al-Isfarayini. These are the primary sources for sectarian views.
These books are considered authoritative.
4
Reflect on the implication
Understanding that only these core works are mentioned suggests that later attributions must be checked against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم نتعرض هنا إلا لأصول الفرق من أهل البدع ولها فروع تتشعب منها على حسب ما يقع فيها من تداخل في الآراء وتجدد في الأهواء وهي لا تنتهي عند عدد محدود إلى انتهاء تاريخ البشر وفي العدد المأثور للعلماء خلاف مشهور، وقد قام العلماء في كل طبقة بتفصيل ما جد إلى عصرهم من أصحاب النحل ورد الباطل من آرائهم. ومقالات تلك الطوائف مبسوطة في مقالات الإسلاميين للأشعري و"المقالات" لأبي منصور الماتريدي و"رد أهل الأهواء والبدع" لأبي الحسين الطرائفي و"الملل والنحل" لأبي المظفر الأسفراييني (1) إلى غير ذلك مما لا يحصى، وكثيرا ما يعزى إلى الفرق أقوال لا توجد في كتبهم إما توليدا وإلزاما ونقلا من كتب غير الثقات من الخصوم كما يقع لعبد القاهر البغدادي في "الفرق بين الفرق" و"الملل والنحل" له (2) وكما يفعل ابن حزم في "الفصل" ومن القبيل الاعتماد على مثل أبي عيسى محمد بن هرون الوراق وأبي محمد الحسن بن موسى النوبختي صاحب "الآراء والديانات"، ومحمد بن إسحاق صاحب "الفهرست" وعلى كتب الحشوية فإنها مملوءة بالمختلقات فشأن الباحث أن يحتاط في نسبة قول إلى قائل حتى يجده في كتاب له مستفيض عنه، وقد نبه على بعض ما تقدم الرازي عند ذكر كتاب الشهرستاني، ولسنا في صدد المقارنة بين كتب الملل والنحل.
We have only mentioned here the roots of the sects of innovators, and they have branches that diverge from them according to the overlap in opinions and renewal of passions, and they do not end at a limited number until the end of human history. There is a well-known disagreement among scholars regarding the counted number. Scholars in every generation have detailed what was new in their time from the people of sects and refuted the falsehood of their opinions. The opinions of those sects are expounded in 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin' by al-Ash'ari and 'al-Maqalat' by Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and 'Raddu Ahl al-Ahwa' wa al-Bida'' by Abu al-Husayn al-Tara'ifi and 'al-Milal wa al-Nihal' by Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini (1) and so on beyond count. Often views are attributed to sects that are not found in their books, either by generation, compulsion, or quotation from unreliable books of opponents, as occurs for 'Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi in 'al-Farq bayna al-Firaq' and 'al-Milal wa al-Nihal' (2) and as Ibn Hazm does in 'al-Fasl'. And of this category is reliance on such as Abu 'Isa Muhammad ibn Harun al-Warraq and Abu Muhammad al-Hasan ibn Musa al-Nawbakhti, author of 'al-Ara' wa al-Diyanat', and Muhammad ibn Ishaq, author of 'al-Fihrist', and the books of the Hashwiyya, for they are filled with fabrications. So it is the business of the researcher to be cautious in attributing a statement to a speaker until he finds it in a book of his widely transmitted from him. And al-Razi has alerted to some of what preceded when mentioning al-Shahristani's book. And we are not in the position of comparing the books of al-Milal wa al-Nihal.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a methodological warning about the attribution of views to heretical sects. The author first notes that he has only covered the main sects, which have many branches. He lists key books on sectarian opinions by al-Ash'ari, al-Maturidi, al-Tara'ifi, and al-Isfarayini. Then he warns that many attributed views are not actually found in the sects' own books, citing examples such as al-Baghdadi and Ibn Hazm, and also unreliable authors like al-Warraq, al-Nawbakhti, and the Hashwiyya. He emphasizes that researchers must be cautious and only attribute a view if it is found in a widely transmitted book of that person. He notes that al-Razi has already pointed this out regarding al-Shahristani's book.

Key Terms
الفرق
أهل البدع
مقالات
الملل والنحل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All books on sects are equally reliable and contain the complete views of the groups.
Correction: The author specifically lists only a few key books as authoritative, implying that others may be less reliable. Many later attributions are not found in the original sources.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the scope of his discussion?
A) All branches of the sects
B) Only the roots of the sects
C) The aqidah of the sects
D) The history of the sects

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author states that scholars in every generation have refuted false opinions. In your own circles, do you speak up against incorrect beliefs about Islam, or do you stay silent? What is one way you can lovingly correct a misconception starting today?
?
The list of books includes works by scholars from different theological backgrounds (Ash'ari, Maturidi). How does this diversity of sources challenge the assumption that there is only one 'correct' Sunni perspective? How can you approach learning about these schools without partisan bias?

Caution Against Unreliable Attributions in Sectarian Studies
Author warns about false attributions and outlines the researcher's duty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the risk of false attributions to sects and the researcher's duty to verify from original widely transmitted works.

Core Idea
Not every attributed view is authentic; verification requires original sources.

After listing reliable sources, the author warns that many views attributed to sects are not found in their own books. He gives examples of scholars who made such errors and identifies unreliable authors. This lesson teaches the critical need for caution in attribution.

Guided Path
1
Read the warning
The passage states that many views are attributed to sects that are not found in their books: 'وكثيرا ما يعزى إلى الفرق أقوال لا توجد في كتبهم'.
This is the core problem.
2
Identify the causes
The passage mentions three ways this happens: توليدا (generation), إلزاما (compulsion), and نقلا من كتب غير الثقات (quoting unreliable opponents).
These are methods of false attribution.
3
Note the examples
The author gives examples: 'Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi, Ibn Hazm, and unreliable authors like al-Warraq, al-Nawbakhti, and the Hashwiyya.
These are scholars whose works contain fabrications.
4
Understand the researcher's rule
The researcher must be cautious: 'فشأن الباحث أن يحتاط في نسبة قول إلى قائل حتى يجده في كتاب له مستفيض عنه' — only attribute a statement if found in a widely transmitted book of that person.
This is the key methodological principle.
5
Reflect on the note about al-Razi
Al-Razi alerted to this problem when mentioning al-Shahristani's book. This shows that the caution is recognized by major scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم نتعرض هنا إلا لأصول الفرق من أهل البدع ولها فروع تتشعب منها على حسب ما يقع فيها من تداخل في الآراء وتجدد في الأهواء وهي لا تنتهي عند عدد محدود إلى انتهاء تاريخ البشر وفي العدد المأثور للعلماء خلاف مشهور، وقد قام العلماء في كل طبقة بتفصيل ما جد إلى عصرهم من أصحاب النحل ورد الباطل من آرائهم. ومقالات تلك الطوائف مبسوطة في مقالات الإسلاميين للأشعري و"المقالات" لأبي منصور الماتريدي و"رد أهل الأهواء والبدع" لأبي الحسين الطرائفي و"الملل والنحل" لأبي المظفر الأسفراييني (1) إلى غير ذلك مما لا يحصى، وكثيرا ما يعزى إلى الفرق أقوال لا توجد في كتبهم إما توليدا وإلزاما ونقلا من كتب غير الثقات من الخصوم كما يقع لعبد القاهر البغدادي في "الفرق بين الفرق" و"الملل والنحل" له (2) وكما يفعل ابن حزم في "الفصل" ومن القبيل الاعتماد على مثل أبي عيسى محمد بن هرون الوراق وأبي محمد الحسن بن موسى النوبختي صاحب "الآراء والديانات"، ومحمد بن إسحاق صاحب "الفهرست" وعلى كتب الحشوية فإنها مملوءة بالمختلقات فشأن الباحث أن يحتاط في نسبة قول إلى قائل حتى يجده في كتاب له مستفيض عنه، وقد نبه على بعض ما تقدم الرازي عند ذكر كتاب الشهرستاني، ولسنا في صدد المقارنة بين كتب الملل والنحل.
We have only mentioned here the roots of the sects of innovators, and they have branches that diverge from them according to the overlap in opinions and renewal of passions, and they do not end at a limited number until the end of human history. There is a well-known disagreement among scholars regarding the counted number. Scholars in every generation have detailed what was new in their time from the people of sects and refuted the falsehood of their opinions. The opinions of those sects are expounded in 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin' by al-Ash'ari and 'al-Maqalat' by Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and 'Raddu Ahl al-Ahwa' wa al-Bida'' by Abu al-Husayn al-Tara'ifi and 'al-Milal wa al-Nihal' by Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini (1) and so on beyond count. Often views are attributed to sects that are not found in their books, either by generation, compulsion, or quotation from unreliable books of opponents, as occurs for 'Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi in 'al-Farq bayna al-Firaq' and 'al-Milal wa al-Nihal' (2) and as Ibn Hazm does in 'al-Fasl'. And of this category is reliance on such as Abu 'Isa Muhammad ibn Harun al-Warraq and Abu Muhammad al-Hasan ibn Musa al-Nawbakhti, author of 'al-Ara' wa al-Diyanat', and Muhammad ibn Ishaq, author of 'al-Fihrist', and the books of the Hashwiyya, for they are filled with fabrications. So it is the business of the researcher to be cautious in attributing a statement to a speaker until he finds it in a book of his widely transmitted from him. And al-Razi has alerted to some of what preceded when mentioning al-Shahristani's book. And we are not in the position of comparing the books of al-Milal wa al-Nihal.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a methodological warning about the attribution of views to heretical sects. The author first notes that he has only covered the main sects, which have many branches. He lists key books on sectarian opinions by al-Ash'ari, al-Maturidi, al-Tara'ifi, and al-Isfarayini. Then he warns that many attributed views are not actually found in the sects' own books, citing examples such as al-Baghdadi and Ibn Hazm, and also unreliable authors like al-Warraq, al-Nawbakhti, and the Hashwiyya. He emphasizes that researchers must be cautious and only attribute a view if it is found in a widely transmitted book of that person. He notes that al-Razi has already pointed this out regarding al-Shahristani's book.

Misconception: Any book that discusses sects is reliable and can be used to attribute views.
Correction: The author explicitly mentions that some books contain fabrications and that even well-known scholars like al-Baghdadi and Ibn Hazm made false attributions.

The author emphasizes that researchers must verify attributions by checking the original sources of the sect in question.

The State of Theological Divisions and al-Ash'ari's Middle Path
Ibn Asakir describes Mu'tazili and Mushabbiha errors and al-Ash'ari's balanced approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two extreme theological positions of ta'til and tashbih, and how Imam al-Ash'ari charted a middle path to preserve divine attributes while avoiding anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari navigated between stripping God of attributes and likening Him to creation.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari sets the historical context for the emergence of the Ash'ari school. It describes how the Mu'tazila denied God's attributes, while the Mushabbiha attributed bodily characteristics to God. The scholars, distressed by these extremes, turned to the Sunnah and discouraged theological speculation. Then Imam al-Ash'ari appears as the defender of the true middle path, using reasoned arguments to uphold the attributes without falling into either error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall picture of Ibn Asakir's historical account.
Notice the vivid imagery: 'market of innovations stood', 'deviated from moderation'.
2
Identify the two extremes
Identify the two groups described: Mu'tazila who negated attributes (ta'til) and Mushabbiha who likened God to creation (tashbih).
3
Analyze al-Ash'ari's response
Notice how Ibn Asakir praises al-Ash'ari as the most concerned and sharpest defender, who imposed proofs on opponents.
The key phrase: 'so he did not go to excess in ta'til nor go to excess in tashbih, and sought between that a middle way.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ركاما وقام سوق البدع عند ولاة المسلمين في الخافقين قياما، وحاد أهل الاعتزال عن سنن الاعتدال جرأة منهم على رد السنن واقداما، فنفوا عن الرب سبحانه ما أثبت لنفسه من صفاته فلم يثبتوا صفة ولا كلاما، وتمادى أهل التشبيه في طرق التمويه وأحجموا عن الحق إحجاما، فشبهوا ربهم حتى توهموه جسما يقبل تحيزا وافتراقا وانضماما، وغلوا في إثبات كلامه حتى حسبوه يحتمل بجهلهم تجزيا وانقساما، وظنوا اسم الله القديم ألفا وهاء تتلو لاما ولاما، فامتعض العلماء من المثبتين من تفاوت مذهبيهم واعتصموا بالسنة اعتصاما، وألجموا العوام عن الخوض في علم الكلام خوف العثار إلجاما، فكان أبو الحسن الأشعري رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه أشدهم بذلك اهتماما، وألدهم لمن حاول الإلحاد في أسماء الله وصفاته خصاما، وأمدهم سنانا لمن عاند السنة، وأحدهم حساما، وأمضاهم جنانا عند وقوع المحنة، وأصعبهم مراما، ألزم الحجة لمن خالف السنة والمحجة إلزاما، فلم يسرف في التعطيل ولم يغل في التشبيه وابتغى بين ذلك قواما.
An accumulation and the market of innovations stood with the rulers of the Muslims in the two horizons standing, and the people of i'tizal deviated from the paths of moderation, out of audacity from them in rejecting the sunnahs and boldness. So they negated from the Lord, glorified be He, what He affirmed for Himself of His attributes, so they did not affirm any attribute nor speech. And the people of tashbih persisted in the ways of obscurity and held back from the truth holding back. So they likened their Lord until they imagined Him a body that accepts spatial location, division, and joining. And they exaggerated in affirming His speech until they thought it could, in their ignorance, admit of partializing and division. And they imagined the eternal name of Allah to be an alif and ha following lam and lam. So the scholars among the affirmers were distressed by the divergence of their two schools and clung to the sunnah clinging, and they muzzled the common people from delving into ilm al-kalam out of fear of stumbling, muzzling. So Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him, was the most concerned among them about that, and the most vehement in argument for the one who attempted heresy regarding Allah's names and attributes, and the sharpest spear among them for the one who opposed the sunnah, and the sharpest sword, and the most penetrating mind at the time of trial, and the most difficult in ambition. He imposed the proof upon the one who opposed the sunnah and the path, imposing, so he did not go to excess in ta'til nor go to excess in tashbih, and sought between that a middle way.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a historical and doctrinal description. Ibn Asakir begins by depicting the state of the Muslim community: innovations flourished, the Mu'tazila deviated from moderation by denying Allah's attributes (ta'til), and the Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists) went to extremes by likening Allah to creation (tashbih), even imagining His name as composed of letters. The scholars, distressed by these extremes, clung to the sunnah and forbade the common people from engaging in kalam. Then Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari emerges as the most concerned, most vehement, sharpest, and most penetrating in defending the sunnah using rational arguments. He imposed proof on opponents and avoided both extremes of ta'til and tashbih, adopting a middle path (qawam).

أبو الحسن الأشعري
السنة
علم الكلام
الاعتدال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Some think al-Ash'ari sided with the Mu'tazila.
Correction: This passage shows he opposed both extremes: he 'did not go to excess in ta'til nor go to excess in tashbih.'

Checkpoint

B) Iman and kufr
C) Qadr and jabr
D) Sunnah and bid'a

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari's theology is a middle path that affirms God's attributes without compromising transcendence or falling into anthropomorphism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone describe Allah in a way that either diminishes His majesty or makes Him sound too human, do you feel the same distress the scholars felt? Or do you remain indifferent? What would it take for you to become as concerned as al-Ash'ari was?
?
The scholars muzzled the common people from debating kalam for fear they would stumble. Yet you are studying these issues right now. Are you doing so with a heart that trembles at the risk of misguidance, or with intellectual arrogance? Which extreme do you personally lean toward — over-thinking or over-simplifying — and how can the middle path of the salaf anchor you?
?
Al-Ash'ari was the most vehement in argument against heresy and the sharpest sword for the sunnah. In your daily conversations, when you hear someone twist Allah's names or attributes, do you speak up with knowledge and wisdom, or do you stay silent? If the former, how can you sharpen your tongue; if the latter, what fear holds you back?

The Dignified Response to Slander
Ibn 'Asakir condemns the slanderers of al-Ash'ari and affirms the victory of truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn 'Asakir's defense of al-Ash'ari and how he contrasts the slanderers' behavior with the dignified response of scholars, while asserting the ultimate triumph of truth.

Core Idea
Truth triumphs over slander when scholars respond with dignity and trust in Allah's help.

In this passage, Ibn 'Asakir defends Imam al-Ash'ari against those who slander him. He describes the tactics of the slanderers and then contrasts them with the noble response of the true scholars. The passage reinforces the conviction that the people of truth will ultimately prevail because Allah is their protector.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's rhythmic prose and strong emotions come through.
The passage uses poetic language and Quranic allusions.
2
Identify the two groups
Notice how Ibn 'Asakir contrasts the slanderers (who mislead, wound, and incite) with the scholars (who respond with generosity and peace). What does this contrast teach?
The scholars' response reflects Islamic adab.
3
Understand the author's motivation and conclusion
Ibn 'Asakir says he wrote this defense due to a request and for reward. He concludes that the people of truth are triumphant because Allah is their helper. Why is this significant?
This reinforces the theme of divine support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He misguides ambiguities and a howler wounds with his tongue the imams of the Muslims and howls ambiguities and causes down from the common people ignorant groups and base throngs, and by his ignorance he incites foolish tyrants to insult the scholars and defame them. But the scholars, when they hear their cunning, count it as a calamity from them, and when they pass by their vulgarity concerning the great imams, they pass generously, and when the ignorant address them they say 'Peace'. Allah will not care about their fabrication concerning Him and their denial of Him, and it will become a binding argument. Were it not for the question of one I saw, whose question had a claim upon me, I would have refrained from mentioning the fall of the ignorant against the imams out of modesty, but I have seized the reward in clarifying the truth concerning the loftiness of his rank. And with what is known of their defamation, the people of truth, praise be to Allah, have become manifest over their enemies and dominant over those who oppose them from the people of innovation, and able to take revenge on those who show enmity out of stubbornness. How could they not be so, while Allah is their Protector and Helper, and He is the best of helpers.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a defense of al-Ash'ari and a condemnation of his detractors. The author begins by describing the slanderers as those who mislead and wound the imams. He then contrasts the behavior of scholars who respond with dignity and peace. He asserts that Allah will not care about the slanders and will make them a binding argument against the slanderers. The author explains that he only wrote this defense because someone asked him, and he hopes for reward. He concludes that the people of truth are triumphant because Allah is their helper.

Acceptance of Repentance from Innovators
Ibn Asakir defends acceptance of repentance from those who led innovation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ibn Asakir argues that repentance from innovation is accepted, even for leaders, and how he refutes objections using reason and revelation.

Core Idea
Innovation is less than shirk; if shirk is forgiven upon repentance, innovation certainly is.

This lesson examines a common objection against accepting the repentance of those who were leaders in innovation. Ibn Asakir responds by showing that the objection lacks evidence, that innovation is not greater than polytheism, and that repentance is accepted from all. Prepare to see how he balances textual proofs and rational consistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection (fain qeel)
Carefully read the objector's statement. What are the main points raised against accepting repentance from a leader in innovation? Note the rhetorical questions and the claim that such repentance is not accepted.
The objector cites weak hadith and common skepticism.
2
Identify the answer's four arguments
In the answer (qulna), Ibn Asakir provides several reasons: the objection lacks proof, the hadith are weak, innovation is less than polytheism, and even zindiq repents. List each argument as you find it.
The key is the comparison with shirk.
3
Reflect on the broader principle
Consider how Ibn Asakir upholds the principle that repentance is always possible unless there is a clear text preventing it. This reflects a balanced approach between hope and fear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : كيف يبرأ من البدعة من كان رأسا فيها وهل يثبت الله من كان كان دهره ينفيها؟ وهل رأيتم بدعيا رجع عن اعتقاد البدعة او حكم لمن اظهر الرجوع منها بصحة الرجعة؟ وقد قيل ان توبة البدعي غير مقبولة وفيئته إلى الحق بعد الضلال ليست بمأمولة، وهب انا قلنا بقبول توبته إذا أظهرها ، أفما ينقص ذلك من رتبته عند من خبرها؟ قلنا هذا قول عرى عن البرهان وقائله بعيد من التحقيق عند الامتحان، بل التوبة مقبولة من كل من تاب والعفو من الله مأمول عن كل من أناب، والأحاديث التي رويت في ذلك غير قوية عند أرباب النقل والقول بذلك مستحيل أيضا من طريق العقل فإن البدعة لا تكون أعظم من الشرك ومن ادعى ذلك فهو من أهل الأفك ومع ذلك فيقبل إسلام الكتابي والمرتد والكافر الأصلي فكيف يستحيل عندكم قبول توبة المبتدع الملى، وقد قال الله عز وجل ان ال لا يغفر ان يشرك به ويغفر مادون ذلك لمن يشاء ) والبدعة إذا كشفت عن حقيقتها وجدتها دون الشرك مما هنالك، فإذا كان يقبل الرجوع عن الشرك الذي لا يغفره فكيف لا تقبل توبة مبتدع لا يشرك به ولا يكفره وأكثر العلماء من أهل التحقيق على القول بقبول توبة الزنديق مع ماينطوي عليه اعتقاده الردىء من الخبث وما يعتقده من جحود الصانع وإنكار البعث والمبتدع لا يجحد الربوبية ولا ينكر العظمة الآلهية، وإنما يترك بعض مايجب عليه أن يعتقده لشبه وقعت له فنكب فيها ،رشده، وقد سمعنا بجماعة من
If it is said: How can one who was a leader in innovation be absolved from innovation? And does Allah establish someone who spent his whole life denying it? And have you seen an innovator who returned from his belief in innovation? Or is it ruled for one who shows repentance from it that his return is valid? And it has been said that the repentance of an innovator is not accepted and his return to truth after misguidance is not to be hoped for. Suppose we do say that his repentance is accepted if he shows it, does that not diminish his rank in the eyes of those who know about it? We say: This statement is bare of proof and its speaker is far from verification upon examination. Rather, repentance is accepted from everyone who repents, and pardon from Allah is hoped for from everyone who turns back. The hadiths reported on this matter are not strong according to the people of transmission, and the statement (that repentance is not accepted) is also impossible from the way of reason. For innovation is not greater than polytheism, and whoever claims that is among the people of falsehood. Despite that, the Islam of a People of the Book, an apostate, and an original disbeliever is accepted. So how can acceptance of repentance of a religious innovator be impossible in your view? And Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, said: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, but He forgives what is less than that to whom He wills.' (Surah an-Nisa 4:48). Innovation, when its reality is uncovered, is found to be less than polytheism in that regard. So if return from polytheism, which He does not forgive, is accepted, then why should the repentance of an innovator who does not associate partners with Him and does not declare Him disbelieved not be accepted? And most of the scholars from the people of verification hold the opinion of accepting the repentance of a heretic (zindiq) despite the evil that his bad belief entails and his denial of the Creator and denial of the resurrection. And the innovator does not deny Lordship nor deny Divine Majesty. He only omits some of what he must believe due to an equivocation that occurred to him, so he strayed in his guidance. And we have heard of a group of
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (فإن قيل/قلنا) dealing with the acceptance of repentance from someone who was a leader in innovation. The objector argues that repentance from innovation, especially for a leader, is not accepted and if accepted it diminishes his rank. The answer refutes this by stating the objection lacks proof. Repentance is accepted from everyone; the hadith cited are weak. Additionally, rationally, innovation is less severe than polytheism (shirk). Since polytheism can be forgiven upon repentance, innovation certainly can. The answer further notes that even the repentance of a zindiq (heretic who denies the Creator) is accepted by most scholars, whereas an innovator does not deny Lordship or Divine Majesty; his error arises from a misconception. Thus, his repentance is even more worthy of acceptance. The passage ends with mention that such turnarounds have been witnessed.

Key Terms
بدعة
توبة
مبتدع
شرك
زنديق
رجوع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that if someone was a leader in innovation, their repentance cannot be accepted or is not truly valid.
Correction: Ibn Asakir demonstrates that repentance is accepted from all, and innovation is less than polytheism, so repentance is certainly accepted.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir's argument, why is repentance from innovation more likely to be accepted than repentance from disbelief?
A) Because innovation is a greater sin
B) Because innovation is less than polytheism
C) Because innovators are already forgiven
D) Because the Prophet prohibited accepting it

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir establishes that repentance from innovation is valid because innovation is less severe than polytheism, and even the repentance of heretics is accepted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever written off someone's repentance because of the gravity of their past sin or the harm they caused to others? How does Ibn Asakir's argument—that even the repentance of a zindiq is accepted—challenge your inner reluctance to accept such repentance? Will you actively work to remove that judgment from your heart starting today?
?
This passage argues that the repentance of a leader in innovation is accepted. Is there a person in your life whose return to the truth you have doubted or dismissed? What would it cost you to sincerely hope for their return and to accept it if they show it? Are you willing to pay that cost?
?
Ibn Asakir says the hadiths against accepting innovator's repentance are weak. Have you ever believed something about Allah's mercy being limited without checking the evidence? What false limits have you placed on Allah's forgiveness, and will you repent from that narrowness right now?
